# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana User Permission Model Role Coverage Audit

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that define and enforce the three-tier permission model (Viewer/Editor/Admin): the role-to-permission mapping, the permission guard middleware, and the folder/dashboard permission inheritance.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Grafana codebase and created a comprehensive answer documenting all Go source files that define and enforce the three-tier permission model (Viewer/Editor/Admin).

## Summary

I found **16 key files** across the codebase that implement the three-tier permission model:

### Core Components:

1. **Role Type Definitions** - Define the basic role hierarchy with precedence (None=10, Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40)

2. **Role-to-Permission Mapping** - Maps each of the three roles to specific actions:
   - Viewer: Read-only actions (dashboards:read, folders:read)
   - Editor: Read + Write/Delete (+ dashboard/folder write and delete)
   - Admin: Full permissions including permissions management

3. **Permission Guard Middleware** - Enforces permissions through:
   - `RoleAuth()`: Simple org role checking
   - `Middleware()`: Full permission evaluation with scope resolution
   - `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()`: Cross-org authorization

4. **Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance** - Automatically includes parent folder permissions via:
   - `GetInheritedScopes()`: Queries folder hierarchy
   - `GetParents()`: Traverses ancestor folders
   - Scope resolvers that include full inheritance chain

The answer.json file contains the complete list of files, 36 key symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining how these components work together to enforce the three-tier permission model throughout Grafana.

Role Type Definitions\\n\\nThe fundamental role types are defined in **pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go** (RoleType, RoleViewer, RoleEditor, RoleAdmin) with a precedence system where Admin > Editor > Viewer > None. The RoleType includes:\\n- `Includes()` method to check role hierarchy\\n- `Children()` and `Parents()` methods for role relationships  \\n- `rolePrecedence` map defining precedence values (10-40)\\n\\nThese are aliased in **pkg/services/org/model.go** for organizational context.\\n\\n## 2. Role-to-Permission Mapping\\n\\nThe core role-to-permission mapping is established in **pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go**:\\n\\n- **BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()**: Creates the three basic roles (Admin, Editor, Viewer) with UIDs like \\\"basic_admin\\\", \\\"basic_editor\\\", \\\"basic_viewer\\\"\\n- **DeclareFixedRoles()**: Registers roles and their permission grants\\n- Uses prefixes: \\\"basic:\\\" for basic roles, \\\"fixed:\\\" for fixed roles, \\\"managed:\\\" for managed roles\\n\\nResource-specific action mappings are defined in:\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go**:\\n- `DashboardViewActions`: READ permissions\\n- `DashboardEditActions`: READ + WRITE + DELETE permissions  \\n- `DashboardAdminActions`: READ + WRITE + DELETE + PERMISSIONS READ/WRITE\\n- `registerDashboardRoles()`: Declares dashboard roles for each tier\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go**:\\n- `FolderViewActions`: READ, ALERTING_READ, LIBRARY_READ, SILENCES_READ\\n- `FolderEditActions`: VIEW + WRITE + DELETE + CREATE dashboards + alerting rules\\n- `FolderAdminActions`: EDIT + PERMISSIONS READ/WRITE\\n- `registerFolderRoles()`: Declares folder roles for each tier\\n\\n## 3. Permission Guard Middleware\\n\\nPermission enforcement is implemented through middleware layers:\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go**:\\n- `Middleware()`: Core permission checking middleware that evaluates actions against user permissions\\n- `authorize()`: Executes evaluator and denies access if evaluation fails\\n- `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()`: Validates user has permissions in target organization\\n- Uses scope injection and mutation for dynamic scopes\\n\\n**pkg/middleware/middleware.go**:\\n- `ReqEditorRole`: Middleware for Editor+Admin role requirement\\n- `ReqOrgAdmin`: Middleware for Admin-only requirement\\n- Basic role authentication middleware definitions\\n\\n**pkg/middleware/auth.go**:\\n- `RoleAuth()`: Simple middleware checking if user's OrgRole matches required roles\\n- Uses `c.OrgRole` to check against allowed roles\\n- `Auth()`: Authentication options middleware\\n- `SnapshotPublicModeOrCreate()`, `SnapshotPublicModeOrDelete()`: Conditional permission checks\\n\\n## 4. Permission Evaluation System\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/evaluator.go**:\\n- `Evaluator` interface: Defines permission evaluation contract\\n- `EvalPermission()`: Creates evaluator checking specific action+scopes\\n- `EvalAll()`: Creates evaluator requiring all sub-evaluators pass\\n- `permissionEvaluator.Evaluate()`: Checks if user permissions match required action/scopes\\n- Implements wildcard matching for scope patterns (e.g., \\\"folders:*\\\")\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/accesscontrol.go**:\\n- `Evaluate()`: Core access control evaluation method\\n- Evaluates permissions after resolving scopes\\n- Handles scope resolution via ScopeAttributeResolvers\\n\\n## 5. Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance\\n\\nPermission inheritance through folder hierarchy:\\n\\n**pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go**:\\n- `GetInheritedScopes()`: Retrieves parent folder scopes for a resource\\n  - Calls `folderSvc.GetParents()` to traverse ancestor folders\\n  - Returns scopes for all ancestor folders in the hierarchy\\n  - Returns nil for General folder (no inheritance)\\n- `NewFolderUIDScopeResolver()`: Scope resolver that includes folder + all ancestor scopes\\n- `NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()`: Dashboard resolver that includes folder hierarchy\\n- `resolveDashboardScope()`: Returns dashboard + folder + ancestor scopes for evaluation\\n\\n**pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder.go**:\\n- `GetParents()` query: Retrieves ancestor folders for a given folder UID\\n- Folder permissions are inherited from parent folders\\n- Comments in code: \\\"if the parent is accessible then the subfolders are accessible as well (due to inheritance)\\\"\\n\\n**pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder_unifiedstorage.go**:\\n- `getAvailableNonRootFolders()`: Filters folders based on user's folder and dashboard permissions\\n- Combines parent folder permissions with dashboard permissions\\n- Handles permission hierarchy: EDIT permissions include READ permissions\\n\\n## 6. Authorization Model\\n\\n**pkg/services/accesscontrol/authorizer.go**:\\n- `ResourceResolver`: Interface for translating resources to scopes\\n- `LegacyAccessClient`: Maps K8s verbs to RBAC actions\\n- Default mapping: Get\u2192read, Create\u2192create, Update\u2192write, Delete\u2192delete, SetPermissions\u2192permissions:write\\n\\n**pkg/api/accesscontrol.go**:\\n- `declareFixedRoles()`: Declares all fixed roles for API operations\\n- Registers roles with their grants to basic org roles\\n- Defines permissions for provisioning, datasources, and other API operations\\n\\n## 7. Scope Model\\n\\nScopes provide fine-grained resource access:\\n- Format: \\\"resource:uid:value\\\" (e.g., \\\"dashboards:uid:my-dashboard\\\", \\\"folders:uid:my-folder\\\")\\n- Wildcards: \\\"folders:*\\\" matches all folders\\n- Providers: ScopeFoldersProvider, ScopeDashboardsProvider for scope generation\\n- Scope hierarchy respects folder/dashboard relationships\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe three-tier permission model flows as:\\n\\n1. **Type Definition**: RoleType enum (pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go)\\n2. **Role Creation**: BuildBasicRoleDefinitions() in roles.go creates Admin/Editor/Viewer\\n3. **Action Mapping**: registerDashboardRoles/registerFolderRoles map actions to roles\\n4. **Middleware Enforcement**: RoleAuth/Middleware in middleware packages check org role\\n5. **Permission Evaluation**: EvalPermission/Evaluate checks actions+scopes against user permissions\\n6. **Inheritance**: GetInheritedScopes includes parent folder scopes in evaluation\\n7. **Authorization**: AccessControl.Evaluate executes the full permission check with scope resolution\"\n}\n",
